## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) is determined by restoring forces (dependent on x), damping (dependent on v), and possibly external driving (dependent on t). The task is to discover the specific nonlinear equation of motion.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (with periodic forcing)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing with damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping)
- Quintic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Softening spring with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (general polynomial restoring force)
- Parametrically driven oscillator: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (time-modulated stiffness)
- Morse-type oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * x) * (1 - exp(c1 * x)) (asymmetric potential)
- Nonlinear damping with driving: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v * x**2 + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (cross-coupled nonlinearity)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (quadratic nonlinearity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium → symmetric potential well
- Even-power restoring forces (x²) break symmetry → asymmetric potential well (Helmholtz-type)
- Velocity-position coupling terms like (1 - x²)*v indicate amplitude-dependent damping → self-sustained oscillations (limit cycles)
- Cubic position terms x³ with same/opposite sign as linear term x indicate hardening/softening spring behavior respectively
- Periodic time dependence cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) in acceleration indicates external periodic driving → possible resonance and chaos
- Odd powers of velocity (v, v³) represent dissipative forces; even powers (v²) can represent direction-dependent drag
- Products x*v indicate phase-space-dependent forces that can transfer energy between kinetic and potential modes
- Absence of explicit time dependence indicates an autonomous system → energy conservation or dissipation without external input
